I have banded over 25,000 birds in my life and I never cease to marvel at what birds look like in the hand. We left Explorers Inn at 3:30 a.m. to hike to Cochachoca Lagoon and arrive before dawn. We then took a small canoe out onto the lagoon, listened to owls & potoos, and watched dawn arive with flights of pigeons & parrots. Just a marvelous experience..... We stayed on lagoon until 9 a.m. (photos of Agami Heron, screamer, etc; heard Long-billed Woodcreeper, yet another potential lifer not included on the checklist) and then hiked in terra firma until early afternoon, returning back to Explorers Inn by 4 p.m.  Nice weather. URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS74003418	11590.39	species	Blue-and-yellow Macaw	Ara ararauna			2			Venezuela	VE	Delta Amacuro	VE-Y				Delta Amacuro	L770923	P	8.603794	-61.6999054	2007-01-15	08:00:00	This was an incredible day, as our group accomplised the following feats:----Firsts ever photographs of the as yet unnamed Wagtail-Tyrant in the wild! ----Only two people (Steve Hilty and David Ascanio) previously had ever seen all 4 of our main targets (Black-chested Tyrant, and the Unnamed Softtail, Spinetail, and Wagtail-Tyrant. We joined only David in seeing all 4 in one day! Thus our group contained EVERYONE who had ever seen all 4 in one day, at the time anyway.----We had just about given up on the Softtail at the location that David thought was our best shot, and were birding our way back to the boat, when a Softtail flew across the trail in front of us. Everyone got great looks, and we got some decent photos. It will be known as the Delta Amacuro Softtail.----Boat trouble early in day robbed us of a lot of time. Late in day we decided to run wide-open to the location that will be the type locality of the Wagtail-Tyrant when it is described, which is a 15km run with practically no time when we get there. As we are on the way, David spots a good-looking island, that he has never stopped at before, but he says it looks perfect. We put all of our hopes on this island. Within minutes David called in a pair of Wagtail-Tyrants, which gave us great looks and we all got photos (the 1st ever).----With only minutes of daylight left, David decided to try for the Spinetail, and about 50 yards farther down he got us that bird as well. (Rio Orinoco Spinetail) Chris managed one shot in the failing light. ----We made most of the ride back in the dark, but easily the most exciting end to a day of birding that I have ever had.----We also heard on the day:----Horned Screamer--Crimson-crested Woodpecker--Plain-crowned Spinetail--Southern Beardless-Tyrannulet--Pale-tipped Inizea--Boat-billed Flycatcher--Scrub Greenlet------	late in day as we were running wide-open to get to our last shot for the Wagtail-Tyrant (and Spinetail) we had two of these beauties fly over.
